     <p><b>The Johns Hopkins University</b><sup id="cite_ref-About_The_Johns_Hopkins_University_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_The_Johns_Hopkins_University-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> (informally <b>Johns Hopkins</b>, <b>JHU</b>, or just <b>Hopkins</b>) is a not-for-profit<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Private_university" title="Private university">private</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. The university was founded on January 22, 1876, and named for its benefactor, the <a href="/wiki/Philanthropist" title="Philanthropist" class="mw-redirect">philanthropist</a> <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins" title="Johns Hopkins">Johns Hopkins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-There_is_only_one_Johns_Hopkins_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-There_is_only_one_Johns_Hopkins-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Coit_Gilman" title="Daniel Coit Gilman">Daniel Coit Gilman</a> was inaugurated as the first <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_(education)#United_States" title="Chancellor (education)">president</a> on February 22, 1876.<sup id="cite_ref-Inaugural_Address_of_Daniel_Coit_Gilman_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inaugural_Address_of_Daniel_Coit_Gilman-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Johns Hopkins maintains campuses in Maryland; <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>; Italy; China and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. The university is organized into two undergraduate divisions and five graduate divisions on two main campuses?the <a href="/wiki/Homewood_Campus_of_Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Homewood Campus of Johns Hopkins University">Homewood campus</a> and the Medical Institutions campus?both located in Baltimore. The university also consists of the <a href="/wiki/Paul_H._Nitze_School_of_Advanced_International_Studies" title="Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies">Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Institute" title="Peabody Institute">Peabody Institute</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carey_Business_School" title="Carey Business School">Carey Business School</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Johns_Hopkins_University_Research_Centers_and_Institutes" title="List of Johns Hopkins University Research Centers and Institutes">various other facilities</a>.</p> 
     <p>Johns Hopkins pioneered the concept of the modern research university in the United States and has ranked among the world's top of such universities throughout its history. The <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> (NSF) has ranked Johns Hopkins #1 among U.S. academic institutions in total science, medical and <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> spending for 31 consecutive years.<sup id="cite_ref-nsf09_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsf09-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2011, thirty-seven <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners have been affiliated with Johns Hopkins,<sup id="cite_ref-The_Johns_Hopkins_University_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Johns_Hopkins_University-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> and the university's research is among the most cited in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-ScienceWatch.com_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScienceWatch.com-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

           <ul> 
            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#The_philanthropist_and_the_founding"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">The philanthropist and the founding</span></a></li>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_philanthropist_and_the_founding">The philanthropist and the founding</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The philanthropist and the founding">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink boilerplate seealso">
      See also: 
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins#Death_and_Philanthropy" title="Johns Hopkins">Johns Hopkins' Philanthropy and Legacy</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hopkinsp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Hopkinsp.jpg/170px-Hopkinsp.jpg" width="170" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Hopkinsp.jpg/255px-Hopkinsp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Hopkinsp.jpg/340px-Hopkinsp.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hopkinsp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins" title="Johns Hopkins">Johns Hopkins</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On his death in 1873, <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins" title="Johns Hopkins">Johns Hopkins</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Quaker" title="Quaker" class="mw-redirect">Quaker</a> <a href="/wiki/Entrepreneur" title="Entrepreneur">entrepreneur</a> and childless bachelor, bequeathed $7 million (between $140 million to $1.6 billion in 2011 dollars, by varying estimates) to fund a hospital and university in Baltimore, Maryland.<sup id="cite_ref-jhu1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jhu1-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> At that time this fortune, generated primarily from the <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Ohio_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Ohio Railroad">Baltimore and Ohio Railroad</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Who_Was_Johns_Hopkins.3F_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Who_Was_Johns_Hopkins.3F-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> was the largest philanthropic gift in the history of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Facts_at_a_Glance_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Facts_at_a_Glance-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The first name of philanthropist Johns Hopkins is the surname of his great-grandmother, Margaret Johns, who married Gerard Hopkins. They named their son Johns Hopkins, who named his own son Samuel Hopkins. Samuel named one of his sons after his father and that son would be the university's benefactor.</p> 
     <p>In his 2001 undergraduate commencement address, university president <a href="/wiki/William_R._Brody" title="William R. Brody">William R. Brody</a> said about the name: &quot;In 1888, just 12 years after the university was founded, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Twain" title="Mark Twain">Mark Twain</a> wrote about this university in a letter to a friend. He said: 'A few months ago I was told that the Johns Hopkins University had given me a degree. I naturally supposed this constituted me a Member of the Faculty and so I started in to help as I could there. I told them I believed they were perfectly competent to run a college as far as the higher branches of education are concerned, but what they needed was a little help here and there from a practical commercial man. I said the public is sensitive to little things and they wouldn't have full confidence in a college that didn't know how to spell the name <i>John</i>.' More than a century later, we continue to bestow diplomas upon individuals of outstanding capabilities and great talent. And we continue to spell <i>Johns</i> with an <i>s</i>.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Commencement_2001_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Commencement_2001-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Milton_Eisenhower" title="Milton Eisenhower" class="mw-redirect">Milton Eisenhower</a>, a former university president, once spoke at a convention in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" title="Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania" class="mw-redirect">Pittsburgh</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Ceremonies" title="Master of Ceremonies" class="mw-redirect">Master of Ceremonies</a> introduced him as &quot;President of <i>John' Hopkins.&quot; Eisenhower retorted that he was &quot;glad to be here in</i> Pitt<i>burgh.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Cheesecake_on_the_Tart_Side_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cheesecake_on_the_Tart_Side-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></i></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_and_Daniel_Coit_Gilman">Early years and Daniel Coit Gilman</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years and Daniel Coit Gilman">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The original board opted for an entirely novel university model dedicated to the discovery of knowledge at an advanced level, extending that of contemporary Germany. Johns Hopkins thereby became the model of the modern research university in the United States. Its success eventually shifted higher education in the United States from a focus on teaching revealed and/or applied knowledge to the scientific discovery of new knowledge. The founders intended the university to be national in scope to strengthen ties across a divided country in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. Therefore, the university's official inauguration took on great significance: 1876 was the nation's centennial year and February 22 was <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>'s birthday.</p> 
     <table class="metadata mbox-small plainlinks" style="border:1px solid #aaa; background-color:#f9f9f9;"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" width="38" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" /></td> 
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style=""><a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">Wikisource</a> has the text of a <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica_Eleventh_Edition" title="Encyclop&aelig;dia Britannica Eleventh Edition">1911 <i>Encyclop&aelig;dia Britannica</i></a> article about <i><b><a href="//en.wikisource.org/wiki/1911_Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica/Johns_Hopkins_University" class="extiw" title="wikisource:1911 Encyclop&aelig;dia Britannica/Johns Hopkins University">the Early History</a></b></i>.</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>The University's viability depended on its first president, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Coit_Gilman" title="Daniel Coit Gilman">Daniel Coit Gilman</a>, recruited from the presidency of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a>. Johns Hopkins was the first American university committed to research following <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt" title="Alexander von Humboldt">Alexander von Humboldt</a>'s ideas of research as practiced at German universities at the time. <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Coit_Gilman" title="Daniel Coit Gilman">Daniel Coit Gilman</a> visited <a href="/wiki/University_of_Freiburg" title="University of Freiburg">University of Freiburg</a> and other German universities in preparation for the founding of Johns Hopkins.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Gilman launched what many at the time considered an audacious and unprecedented academic experiment to merge teaching and research. He dismissed the idea that the two were mutually exclusive: &quot;The best teachers are usually those who are free, competent and willing to make original researches in the library and the laboratory,&quot; he stated. To implement his plan, Gilman recruited internationally known luminaries such as the biologist <a href="/wiki/H._Newell_Martin" title="H. Newell Martin">H. Newell Martin</a>; the physicist <a href="/wiki/Henry_Augustus_Rowland" title="Henry Augustus Rowland">Henry A. Rowland</a> (the first president of the <a href="/wiki/American_Physical_Society" title="American Physical Society">American Physical Society</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Classical_scholars" title="Classical scholars" class="mw-redirect">classical scholars</a> <a href="/wiki/Basil_Gildersleeve" title="Basil Gildersleeve" class="mw-redirect">Basil Gildersleeve</a> and Charles D. Morris;<sup id="cite_ref-university_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-university-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> the economist <a href="/wiki/Richard_T._Ely" title="Richard T. Ely">Richard T. Ely</a>; and the chemist <a href="/wiki/Ira_Remsen" title="Ira Remsen">Ira Remsen</a>, who became the second president of the university in 1901.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Daniel_Coit_Gilman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/86/Daniel_Coit_Gilman.jpg/170px-Daniel_Coit_Gilman.jpg" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/86/Daniel_Coit_Gilman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/86/Daniel_Coit_Gilman.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Daniel_Coit_Gilman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Coit_Gilman" title="Daniel Coit Gilman">Daniel Coit Gilman</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Gilman focused on the expansion of knowledge, graduate education and support of faculty research. To Gilman, Johns Hopkins existed not for the sake of God, the state, the community, the board, the parents, or even the students, but for knowledge. Faculty who added to such knowledge were rewarded. A complementary focus on <a href="/wiki/Graduate_education" title="Graduate education" class="mw-redirect">graduate education</a> fused advanced scholarship with such professional schools as medicine and engineering. Hopkins became the national trendsetter in <a href="/wiki/PhD" title="PhD" class="mw-redirect">doctoral</a> programs and the host for numerous <a href="/wiki/Scholarly_journal" title="Scholarly journal" class="mw-redirect">scholarly journals</a> and associations with the founding of the first U.S. <a href="/wiki/University_press" title="University press" class="mw-redirect">university press</a> in 1878.</p> 
     <p>With the completion of <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">Johns Hopkins Hospital</a> in 1889 and the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">medical school</a> in 1893, the university's research?focused mode of instruction soon began attracting world-renowned faculty members who would become major figures in the emerging field of academic medicine, including <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">William Osler</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Halsted" title="William Halsted" class="mw-redirect">William Halsted</a>, <a href="/wiki/Howard_Kelly" title="Howard Kelly" class="mw-redirect">Howard Kelly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/William_H._Welch" title="William H. Welch">William Welch</a>. During this period Hopkins made more history by becoming the first medical school to admit women on an equal basis with men and to require a <a href="/wiki/Bachelors_degree" title="Bachelors degree" class="mw-redirect">Bachelors degree</a>, based on the efforts of <a href="/wiki/Mary_Garrett" title="Mary Garrett">Mary E. Garrett</a>, who had endowed the school at Gilman's request.</p> 
     <p>In his will and in his instructions to the trustees of the university and the hospital, Hopkins requested that both institutions be built upon the vast grounds of his Baltimore estate, Clifton. When Gilman assumed the presidency, he decided that it would be best to use the university's endowment for recruiting faculty and students, deciding to &quot;build men, not buildings.&quot; In his will Hopkins stipulated that none of his endowment should be used for construction; only interest on the principal could be used for this purpose. Unfortunately, stocks in The <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Ohio_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Ohio Railroad">Baltimore and Ohio Railroad</a>, which would have generated most of the interest, became virtually worthless soon after Hopkins's death. The university's first home was thus in Downtown Baltimore delaying plans to site the university in Clifton. This decision became the only major criticism of Gilman's presidency. In the early 20th century the university outgrew its buildings and the trustees began to search for a new home. Developing Clifton for the university was too costly, and so the estate became a public park. In the end, the 140 acres (57&nbsp;ha) estate in north Baltimore known as <a href="/wiki/Homewood_campus" title="Homewood campus" class="mw-redirect">Homewood</a> was purchased as the university's new campus with assistance from prominent Baltimore citizens.</p> 
     <p>Since the 1910s, Johns Hopkins University has famously been a &quot;fertile cradle&quot; to <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Lovejoy" title="Arthur Lovejoy" class="mw-redirect">Arthur Lovejoy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/History_of_ideas" title="History of ideas">history of ideas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Paulson1970_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paulson1970-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin:10px">

        <td><a href="/wiki/Ronald_J._Daniels" title="Ronald J. Daniels">Ronald J. Daniels</a></td> 
        <td>March 2009?Present</td> 
       </tr>

     </table> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institutions">Institutions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Institutions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_Press" title="Johns Hopkins University Press">Johns Hopkins University Press</a>, founded in 1878, is the oldest American <a href="/wiki/University_press" title="University press" class="mw-redirect">university press</a> in continuous operation. Along with the hospital, Hopkins established one of the nation's oldest <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Nursing" title="Johns Hopkins School of Nursing">schools of nursing</a> in 1889. The <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">school of medicine</a> was America's first coeducational, graduate-level medical school, and was a prototype for academic medicine that emphasized bedside learning, research projects, and laboratory training. In 1909, the university was among the first to start adult <a href="/wiki/Continuing_education" title="Continuing education">continuing education</a> programs and in 1916 it founded the US' first <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Bloomberg_School_of_Public_Health" title="Johns Hopkins Bloomberg School of Public Health">school of public health</a>. Programs in international studies and the performing arts were established in 1950 and 1977 when the <a href="/wiki/Paul_H._Nitze_School_of_Advanced_International_Studies" title="Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies">Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies</a> in Washington D.C and the <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Institute" title="Peabody Institute">Peabody Institute</a> in Baltimore became divisions of the university.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_rights">Civil rights</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Civil rights">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="African-Americans">African-Americans</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: African-Americans">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Hopkins was a prominent <a href="/wiki/Abolitionist" title="Abolitionist" class="mw-redirect">abolitionist</a> who supported <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> during the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. After his death, reports said his conviction was a decisive factor in enrolling Hopkins' first <a href="/wiki/African-American" title="African-American" class="mw-redirect">African-American</a> student, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Miller_(scientist)" title="Kelly Miller (scientist)">Kelly Miller</a>, a graduate student in physics, astronomy and mathematics, and in admitting Harvard-trained physician Whitfield Winsey and two other African-American physicians to Maryland's Medical and Chirurgical Society <a href="/wiki/MedChi" title="MedChi">MedChi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mdhistoryonline_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mdhistoryonline-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> These physicians could attend meetings only because they were held on campus. As the memory of Hopkins faded and trustees like King died, Hopkins became like other Baltimore institutions, particularly in terms of race. The Johns Hopkins University chronology stated that on March 15, 1892, an administrator hired by Gilman recommended that the hospital should have a &quot;?separate ward for colored patients.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-webapps.jhu.edu_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webapps.jhu.edu-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Johns Hopkins Hospital subsequently became segregated. Johns Hopkins' &quot;separate but equal&quot; stance was evident when it came to these segregated wards: &quot;Special care will be taken to see that the heating and ventilation apparatus is as perfect as possible. A sun balcony will be erected on each floor on the east side, for convalescents, while a sun bay-window will be constructed at the south end of the south wing. On each floor there will be a dining room, kitchen, lavatory and bath-rooms...The building will be <a href="/wiki/Fireproof" title="Fireproof" class="mw-redirect">fireproof</a> throughout.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-webapps.jhu.edu_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webapps.jhu.edu-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As segregation grew within Johns Hopkins institutions, it affected pay, hiring and promotions. Staff in segregated wards and those employed in the lower rungs of the service industries had the longest history within the Johns Hopkins Institutions. Johns Hopkins' students, physicians, administrators and staff of African descent had a much shorter history within these institutions. The first black undergraduate was Frederick Scott who entered the school in 1945. In 1967 the first black students earned graduate degrees. Dr. James Nabwangu a British-trained <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenyan</a>, was the first black graduate of the medical school. A second was earned by Robert Gamble.<sup id="cite_ref-In_a_Sea_of_White_Faces_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-In_a_Sea_of_White_Faces-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The first African-American instructor was laboratory supervisor <a href="/wiki/Vivien_Thomas" title="Vivien Thomas">Vivien Thomas</a>, who also invented and developed research instruments, served as an assistant in surgery to surgeon <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Blalock" title="Alfred Blalock">Alfred Blalock</a> and worked closely with Blalock and <a href="/wiki/Helen_Taussig" title="Helen Taussig" class="mw-redirect">Helen Taussig</a> in developing and conducting the first successful <a href="/wiki/Blue_baby_syndrome" title="Blue baby syndrome">blue baby operation</a>. Black students and professionals were rare at Johns Hopkins Institutions and Maryland's state medical societies until after the 1940s. Diversity increased only in the 1960s and 1970s. African-Americans and women were labeled &quot;The Uninvited&quot; in the second major history of the university.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Women">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>Hopkins' most well?known battle for women's rights was the one led by daughters of trustees of the university; <a href="/wiki/Mary_Garrett" title="Mary Garrett">Mary E. Garrett</a>, <a href="/wiki/M._Carey_Thomas" title="M. Carey Thomas">M. Carey Thomas</a>, Mamie Gwinn, Elizabeth King, and Julia Rogers.<sup id="cite_ref-women_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> They donated and raised the funds needed to open the medical school, and required Hopkins' officials to agree to their stipulation that women would be admitted. Unfortunately, this stipulation applied only to the medical school. Other graduate schools were opened to women by president <a href="/wiki/Ira_Remsen" title="Ira Remsen">Ira Remsen</a> only in 1907. <a href="/wiki/Christine_Ladd-Franklin" title="Christine Ladd-Franklin">Christine Ladd-Franklin</a> was the first woman to earn a <a href="/wiki/PhD" title="PhD" class="mw-redirect">PhD</a> at Hopkins, in mathematics in 1882. The trustees denied her the degree and refused to change the policy about admitting women; she finally received her degree 44 years later. In 1893 Florence Bascomb became the university's first female PhD.<sup id="cite_ref-women_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-women-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Nursing_school" title="Nursing school">nursing school</a> opened in 1889 and accepted women and men as students.</p> 
     <p>The decision to admit women at undergraduate level was not considered until the late 1960s and was eventually adopted in October 1969; in the fall of 1970, 90 females, five of them African-American, became undergraduates. In the academic year 1970?1971, 4.7% of students in the Arts and Sciences programs were women. In the year 1985?1986 the proportion of female students in the Arts and Sciences programs had increased to around 38%. As of 2009?2010, the undergraduate population was 47% female and 53% male.<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_University_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_University-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a>]</span></h2>

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Homewood">Homewood</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Homewood">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Homewood_Campus_of_Johns_Hopkins_University" title="Homewood Campus of Johns Hopkins University">Homewood Campus of Johns Hopkins University</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JHU-H.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/JHU-H.jpg/220px-JHU-H.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/JHU-H.jpg/330px-JHU-H.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/JHU-H.jpg/440px-JHU-H.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JHU-H.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Homewood House
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Zanvyl_Krieger_School_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Zanvyl Krieger School of Arts and Sciences" class="mw-redirect">Zanvyl Krieger School of Arts and Sciences</a></b>: The Krieger School offers more than 60 undergraduate majors and minors and more than 40 graduate programs.<sup id="cite_ref-Krieger_School_of_Arts_.26_Sciences_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krieger_School_of_Arts_.26_Sciences-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Whiting_School_of_Engineering" title="Whiting School of Engineering">G.W.C. Whiting School of Engineering</a></b>: The Whiting School contains 14 undergraduate and graduate engineering programs and 12 additional areas of study.<sup id="cite_ref-Departments_.26_Areas_of_Study_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Departments_.26_Areas_of_Study-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_School_of_Education" title="Johns Hopkins University School of Education" class="mw-redirect">School of Education</a></b>: Originally established in 1909 as The School of Professional Studies in Business and Education, the divisions of Education and Business became separate schools in 2007.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The first campus was located on Howard Street. Eventually, they relocated to Homewood, in northern Baltimore, the estate of Charles Carroll, son of the oldest surviving signer of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>. Carroll's <a href="/wiki/Homewood_House" title="Homewood House" class="mw-redirect">Homewood House</a> is considered one of the finest examples of Federal residential architecture. The estate then came to the Wyman family, which participated in making it the park-like main campus of the schools of arts and sciences and engineering at the start of the 20th century. Most of its architecture was modeled after the <a href="/wiki/Federal_architecture" title="Federal architecture">Federal style</a> of <a href="/wiki/Homewood_House" title="Homewood House" class="mw-redirect">Homewood House</a>. Homewood House is preserved as a museum. Most undergraduate programs are on this campus.<br style="clear:both;" /></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Baltimore">East Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: East Baltimore">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Hopkins_hospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d4/Hopkins_hospital.jpg/220px-Hopkins_hospital.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d4/Hopkins_hospital.jpg/330px-Hopkins_hospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d4/Hopkins_hospital.jpg/440px-Hopkins_hospital.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Hopkins_hospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         Johns Hopkins Hospital
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Collectively known as Johns Hopkins Medical Institutions (JHMI) campus, the East Baltimore facility occupies several city blocks spreading from the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">Johns Hopkins Hospital</a> trademark dome.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a></b>: The School of Medicine is widely regarded as one of the best medical schools and <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_research" title="Biomedical research" class="mw-redirect">biomedical research</a> institutes in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Biological_Sciences_Graduate_Schools_Rankings_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Biological_Sciences_Graduate_Schools_Rankings-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Medical_School_Research_Rankings_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Medical_School_Research_Rankings-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Bloomberg_School_of_Public_Health" title="Bloomberg School of Public Health" class="mw-redirect">Bloomberg School of Public Health</a></b>: The Bloomberg School was founded in 1916, the world's first and largest public health school. It has consistently been ranked first in its field.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Public_Health_Graduate_Schools_Rankings_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Public_Health_Graduate_Schools_Rankings-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Nursing" title="Johns Hopkins School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a></b>: The School of Nursing is one of America's oldest and pre-eminent schools for nursing education. It has consistently ranked first in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Nursing_Graduate_Schools_Rankings_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Nursing_Graduate_Schools_Rankings-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><br style="clear:both;" /></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_Baltimore">Downtown Baltimore</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Downtown Baltimore">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Peabody_Institute,_Mount_Vernon_Place,_Baltimore,_MD.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Peabody_Institute%2C_Mount_Vernon_Place%2C_Baltimore%2C_MD.jpg/220px-Peabody_Institute%2C_Mount_Vernon_Place%2C_Baltimore%2C_MD.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Peabody_Institute%2C_Mount_Vernon_Place%2C_Baltimore%2C_MD.jpg/330px-Peabody_Institute%2C_Mount_Vernon_Place%2C_Baltimore%2C_MD.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Peabody_Institute%2C_Mount_Vernon_Place%2C_Baltimore%2C_MD.jpg/440px-Peabody_Institute%2C_Mount_Vernon_Place%2C_Baltimore%2C_MD.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Peabody_Institute,_Mount_Vernon_Place,_Baltimore,_MD.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Peabody Institute
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Carey_Business_School" title="Carey Business School">Carey Business School</a></b>: The Carey Business School was established in 2007, incorporating divisions of the former School of Professional Studies in Business and Education. It was originally located on <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Route_139" title="Maryland Route 139" class="mw-redirect">Charles Street</a>, but relocated to the Legg Mason building in Harbor East in 2011.</li> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Peabody_Institute" title="Peabody Institute">Peabody Institute</a></b>: founded in 1857, is the oldest continuously active music conservatory in the United States; it became a division of Johns Hopkins in 1977. The Conservatory retains its own student body and grants degrees in musicology and performance, though both Hopkins and Peabody students may take courses at both institutions. It is located on East Mount Vernon Place.<br style="clear:both;" /></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Washington.2C_D.C.">Washington, D.C.</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Washington, D.C.">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:SAIS_front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/SAIS_front.jpg/220px-SAIS_front.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/SAIS_front.jpg/330px-SAIS_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/SAIS_front.jpg/440px-SAIS_front.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:SAIS_front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Washington D.C. Campus (SAIS)
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Paul_H._Nitze_School_of_Advanced_International_Studies" title="Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies">Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies</a> (SAIS)</b> is located on the Washington D.C. campus near <a href="/wiki/Dupont_Circle" title="Dupont Circle">Dupont Circle</a>. SAIS is devoted to international studies, particularly <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy" title="Diplomacy">diplomacy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">economics</a>. SAIS has full-time international campuses in <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Center" title="Bologna Center" class="mw-redirect">Bologna, Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hopkins-Nanjing_Center" title="Hopkins-Nanjing Center" class="mw-redirect">Nanjing, China</a>. Founded in 1943, SAIS became a part of the university in 1950. In a 2005 survey 65% of respondents ranked SAIS as the nation's top <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_Degree" title="Master's Degree" class="mw-redirect">Master's Degree</a> program in <a href="/wiki/International_Relations" title="International Relations" class="mw-redirect">International Relations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-.27saistop.27_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.27saistop.27-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Zanvyl_Krieger_School_of_Arts_and_Sciences#Advanced_Academic_Programs" title="Zanvyl Krieger School of Arts and Sciences" class="mw-redirect">The Krieger School of Arts and Sciences' Advanced Academic Programs (AAP)</a><sup id="cite_ref-Campuses_.26_Centers_.E2.80.93_The_Washington_DC_Center_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Campuses_.26_Centers_.E2.80.93_The_Washington_DC_Center-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Carey_Business_School" title="Carey Business School">Carey Business School</a></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The Washington, D.C. campus is on <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Avenue_(Washington,_D.C.)" title="Massachusetts Avenue (Washington, D.C.)">Massachusetts Avenue</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Laurel.2C_Maryland">Laurel, Maryland</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Laurel, Maryland">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg/220px-New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg/330px-New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg/440px-New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:New_Horizons_LORRI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Installing a 
        <a href="/wiki/New_Horizons" title="New Horizons">New Horizons</a> Imager at the APL
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li><b><a href="/wiki/Applied_Physics_Laboratory" title="Applied Physics Laboratory">Johns Hopkins University Applied Physics Laboratory (APL)</a></b>: The APL in Laurel, Maryland, specializes in research for the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">U.S. Department of Defense</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> and other government and civilian research agencies. It has developed more than 100 biomedical devices, many in collaboration with the Johns Hopkins Medical Institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-The_125th_Anniversary_of_The_Johns_Hopkins_University_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_125th_Anniversary_of_The_Johns_Hopkins_University-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The Applied Physics Laboratory, a division of the university co-equal to the nine schools but with a non-academic mission, lies between Baltimore and Washington in <a href="/wiki/Laurel,_Maryland" title="Laurel, Maryland">Laurel</a>, Maryland.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_campuses">Other campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other campuses">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <dl> 
      <dd>
       <i>see also <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University#Research_centers_and_institutes" title="Johns Hopkins University">List of Johns Hopkins University Research Centers and Institutes</a></i>
      </dd> 
     </dl> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic">Domestic</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Domestic">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Columbia,_Maryland" title="Columbia, Maryland">Columbia, Maryland Center</a> (Branches of <a href="/wiki/Carey_Business_School" title="Carey Business School">The Carey Business School</a><sup id="cite_ref-Columbia_Center_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Columbia_Center-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_School_of_Education" title="Johns Hopkins University School of Education" class="mw-redirect">The School of Education</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-School_of_Education_at_Johns_Hopkins_University-Columbia_Center_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-School_of_Education_at_Johns_Hopkins_University-Columbia_Center-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Montgomery_County,_Maryland" title="Montgomery County, Maryland">Montgomery County</a>, Maryland Campus (Part-time programs in Biosciences, Engineering, Business &amp; Education<sup id="cite_ref-index_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International">International</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: International">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Bologna_Center" title="Bologna Center" class="mw-redirect">The SAIS Bologna Center, Italy</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Hopkins-Nanjing_Center" title="Hopkins-Nanjing Center" class="mw-redirect">The SAIS Hopkins-Nanjing Center for Chinese and American Studies, China</a></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore#Yong_Siew_Toh_Conservatory_of_Music" title="National University of Singapore">Yong Siew Toh Conservatory of Music</a> (Collaboration between the <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Institute" title="Peabody Institute">Peabody Institute</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a>)</li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>In 2009, JHU ranked fifth among US universities in private fund?raising, collecting <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>433.39 million.<sup id="cite_ref-cae_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cae-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The President is JHU's chief executive officer, and the university is organized into nine academic divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_environmental_initiatives">Campus environmental initiatives</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Campus environmental initiatives">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Johns Hopkins University has implemented a number of <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-.272008_JHU_Sustainability_Initiatives.27_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.272008_JHU_Sustainability_Initiatives.27-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2011, the <i>Sustainable Endowments Institute</i> gave Johns Hopkins a College Sustainability Report Card grade of &quot;C+.&quot; In particular the Institute criticized JHU for failing to disclose its endowment's holdings and proxy voting record on environmental issues.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2007 carbon emissions were inventoried and electric vehicles were used for some campus transportation needs.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As of 2007 dining services managers sought locally?sourced produce and seafood, and integrated organic food into menus.<sup id="cite_ref-.272007-sustainability-report.27_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.272007-sustainability-report.27-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, the smaller caf&eacute;s around campus sell exclusively organic, shade?grown coffees. A small pilot composting program operated on the undergraduate campus.<sup id="cite_ref-.272007-sustainability-report.27_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.272007-sustainability-report.27-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Buildings">Buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Buildings">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2007 the university was pursuing <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> certification for several buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-.272007-sustainability-report.27_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.272007-sustainability-report.27-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Energy retrofits in certain buildings have resulted in over 50% less energy consumption.<sup id="cite_ref-.272007-sustainability-report.27_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.272007-sustainability-report.27-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Retrofits included a green roof, experimentation with waterless <a href="/wiki/Urinal_(restroom)" title="Urinal (restroom)" class="mw-redirect">urinals</a> and low-flow shower heads, and upgraded <a href="/wiki/Fluorescent" title="Fluorescent" class="mw-redirect">fluorescent</a> lighting that reduced electricity for lighting on one campus by over 40 percent. Similar lighting retrofits were underway at all campuses. At the beginning of 2012, Hopkins sustainability announced the installation of 2,708 solar panels atop buildings at Homewood (Rec/Athletic Center, Mattin Center), the Eastern Building on 33rd Street and the East Baltimore Campus (Pinkard Building, 2024 Building, Bloomberg Building, Hampton House). These solar panels will produce 997,400 kWh and decrease 1,200,000&nbsp;lbs of greenhouse gases each year.<sup id="cite_ref-.27Solar_Energy_at_Hopkins.27_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.27Solar_Energy_at_Hopkins.27-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2004, one campus completed a water conservation retrofit that annually saved over 8,000,000 US gallons (30,000,000&nbsp;l) of water.<sup id="cite_ref-.272007-sustainability-report.27_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.272007-sustainability-report.27-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_support">Student support</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Student support">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As of 2010 students contributed significantly to environmental initiatives, setting up the JHU recycling program, hosting a national &quot;Greening&quot; conference, launching a transportation shuttle service between campuses and making the campus more bike-friendly.<sup id="cite_ref-.272008_JHU_Sustainability_Initiatives.27_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-.272008_JHU_Sustainability_Initiatives.27-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> Each year, students conduct the &quot;S.E.X.:I.T.&quot; competition to see which dormitory can save the most electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorm_Competitions_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorm_Competitions-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The Johns Hopkins entity is structured as two corporations, the university and The Johns Hopkins Health System, formed in 1986. The latter has grown into the bigger entity, with fiscal year 2005 consolidated net revenue of $3.3 billion, employing 27,700 people, including some 4,700 full?time physicians.<sup id="cite_ref-overview_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-overview-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>JHU's bylaws specify a Board of Trustees of between 18 and 65 voting members. Trustees serve six?year terms subject to a two?term limit. The alumni select 12 trustees. Four recent alumni serve 4-year terms, one per year, typically from the graduating class. The bylaws prohibit students, faculty or administrative staff from serving on the Board, except the President as an ex?officio trustee.<sup id="cite_ref-Bylaws_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bylaws-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The Johns Hopkins Health System has a separate Board of Trustees, many of whom are doctors or health care executives. Some JHU Trustees also serve on the Johns Hopkins Health System Board.<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_Medicine_Adds_Four_to_Board_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_Medicine_Adds_Four_to_Board-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JHU-Z.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7a/JHU-Z.jpg/220px-JHU-Z.jpg" width="220" height="67" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7a/JHU-Z.jpg/330px-JHU-Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7a/JHU-Z.jpg/440px-JHU-Z.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JHU-Z.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Mason Hall, the Visitor's Center &amp; Admissions Office at Johns Hopkins University
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The full-time, four-year undergraduate program is &quot;most selective&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_University_.E2.80.93_Best_Colleges_.E2.80.93_Education_.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_University_.E2.80.93_Best_Colleges_.E2.80.93_Education_.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> with low transfer-in and a high graduate co-existence.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The cost of attendance per year is $60,820; however, the average need met is 99%.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is one of fourteen founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (AAU); it is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Consortium_on_Financing_Higher_Education" title="Consortium on Financing Higher Education">Consortium on Financing Higher Education</a> (COFHE) and the <a href="/wiki/Universities_Research_Association" title="Universities Research Association">Universities Research Association</a> (URA).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Undergraduate_admissions">Undergraduate admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Undergraduate admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <table style="text-align:center; float:right; font-size:85%; margin-left:2em; margin:10px;" class="wikitable"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <th colspan="2">Johns Hopkins University<sup id="cite_ref-Applications_up_14_percent_for_incoming_Homewood_class_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Applications_up_14_percent_for_incoming_Homewood_class-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JHUGazette2012_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JHUGazette2012-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
       </tr> 
       <tr>

       </tr> 
       <tr>

        <td style="text-align:center;">3,632 (17.7%)</td> 
       </tr>

       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>In 2010, 87% of admitted students graduated in the top tenth of their high school class and the inter-quartile range on the <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> reading was 670?750, math was 690?780, and writing was 670?770. 97% of freshmen returned after the first year, 84% of students graduated in 4 years and 92% graduated in 6 years.<sup id="cite_ref-CDS_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CDS-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> The average GPA of enrolled freshmen is 3.74. Over time, applications to Johns Hopkins University have risen steadily. As a result, the selectivity of Johns Hopkins University has also increased. <a href="/wiki/Early_Decision" title="Early Decision" class="mw-redirect">Early Decision</a> is an option at Johns Hopkins University for students who wish to demonstrate that the university is their first choice. These students, if admitted, are required to enroll. This application is due November 1. Most students, however, apply Regular Decision, which is a traditional non-binding round. These applications are due January 1 and students are notified April 1.</p>
