     </table> 
     <p>At the undergraduate level, Hopkins was ranked <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>13 among National Universities by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a> (USNWR)</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-America.27s_Best_Colleges_2010:_National_Universities_Rankings_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-America.27s_Best_Colleges_2010:_National_Universities_Rankings-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> It is ranked <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>1 in the nation in the high school counselor reputation rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-HS_Counselor_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HS_Counselor-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The 2012 <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU)</i> ranked Hopkins <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>17 internationally (<sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>15 nationally) and 3rd in the world for Clinical Medicine and Pharmacy.<sup id="cite_ref-shanghai2_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shanghai2-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, Johns Hopkins ranked 13th in the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-World_University_Rankings_2010.E2.80.9311_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_University_Rankings_2010.E2.80.9311-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> and 16th in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_World_University_Rankings_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS_World_University_Rankings-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-World_University_Rankings_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_University_Rankings-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Top_200_World_Universities_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_200_World_Universities-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Johns Hopkins also placed <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>2 in the 2010 University Ranking by Academic Performance (URAP),<sup id="cite_ref-2010_University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance_.28URAP.29_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance_.28URAP.29-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>2 in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/HEEACT_%E2%80%93_Performance_Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers_for_World_Universities" title="HEEACT ? Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities" class="mw-redirect">HEEACT ? Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-World_Universities_Rankings_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-World_Universities_Rankings-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>7 among Top Performing Schools according to the <i><a href="/wiki/Faculty_Scholarly_Productivity_Index" title="Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index">Faculty Scholarly Productivity Index</a> (FSPI)</i> in 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-Top_Schools_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Schools-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> and was listed <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>9 among research universities by the <i><a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a></i> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_American_Research_Universities_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_American_Research_Universities-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>For <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> research <i>U.S. News and World Report</i> ranks the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a> <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>2<sup id="cite_ref-America.27s_Best_Graduate_Schools_2011:_Top_Medical_Schools_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-America.27s_Best_Graduate_Schools_2011:_Top_Medical_Schools-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> and has consistently ranked the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Bloomberg_School_of_Public_Health" title="Johns Hopkins Bloomberg School of Public Health">Bloomberg School of Public Health</a> <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>1<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Public_Health_Graduate_Schools_Rankings2_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Public_Health_Graduate_Schools_Rankings2-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> in the nation. The <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Nursing" title="Johns Hopkins School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a> was ranked <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>1 nationally among peer institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Nursing_Graduate_Schools_Rankings3_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Nursing_Graduate_Schools_Rankings3-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Times Higher Education Supplement</i> ranked Johns Hopkins University <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>3 in the world for <a href="/wiki/Biomedicine" title="Biomedicine">biomedicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Life_sciences" title="Life sciences">life sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_Universities_QS_World_University_Rankings_2008:_Life_Sciences_and_Biomedicine_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_Universities_QS_World_University_Rankings_2008:_Life_Sciences_and_Biomedicine-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Hopkins ranks <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>1 nationally in receipt of federal research funds and the School of Medicine is <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>1 among medical schools in receipt of extramural awards from the <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">National Institutes of Health (NIH)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_University_Facts_at_a_Glance_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_University_Facts_at_a_Glance-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Newsweek named Johns Hopkins as the &quot;Hottest School for Pre-meds&quot; in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-25_Hottest_Schools_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25_Hottest_Schools-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">Johns Hopkins Hospital</a> was ranked as the top hospital in the United States for the eighteenth year in a row by the <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i> annual ranking of American hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Hospital_Rankings_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S._News_.26_World_Report:_Best_Hospital_Rankings-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's graduate programs in the areas of <a href="/wiki/Biological_science" title="Biological science" class="mw-redirect">Biological</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Biomedical_science" title="Biomedical science" class="mw-redirect">Biomedical Sciences</a>, Engineering (<a href="/wiki/Biomedical_engineering" title="Biomedical engineering">Biomedical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">Electrical</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Environmental_engineering" title="Environmental engineering">Environmental</a>), <a href="/wiki/Developmental_psychology" title="Developmental psychology">Human Development</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Sociology_of_the_family" title="Sociology of the family">Family Studies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_Sciences" title="Health Sciences" class="mw-redirect">Health Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">Humanities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physical_sciences" title="Physical sciences" class="mw-redirect">Physical</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Mathematical_Sciences" title="Mathematical Sciences" class="mw-redirect">Mathematical Sciences</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">International Affairs</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/International_Development" title="International Development" class="mw-redirect">Development</a> all rank among the top-10 of their respective disciplines.<sup id="cite_ref-2007_Faculty_Scholarly_Productivity_Index:_Johns_Hopkins_University_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2007_Faculty_Scholarly_Productivity_Index:_Johns_Hopkins_University-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AA_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AA-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Paul_H._Nitze_School_of_Advanced_International_Studies" title="Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies">Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies</a> (SAIS) ranked #1 (2005), #2 (2007), and #2 (2009), by <a href="/wiki/College_of_William_and_Mary" title="College of William and Mary" class="mw-redirect">College of William and Mary</a>'s surveys conducted once every two years beginning in 2005, for its MA program among the world's top schools of International Affairs for those who want to pursue a policy career.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_School_of_Education" title="Johns Hopkins University School of Education" class="mw-redirect">School of Education</a> is ranked <sup><span style="font-variant:small-caps">#</span></sup>2 nationally by <i>U.S. News and World Report</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_.E2.80.93_Best_Education_Schools_.E2.80.93_Graduate_Schools_.E2.80.93_Education_.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_.E2.80.93_Best_Education_Schools_.E2.80.93_Graduate_Schools_.E2.80.93_Education_.E2.80.93_US_News_and_World_Report-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> Although no formal rankings exist for <a href="/wiki/Music_school" title="Music school">music conservatories</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Peabody_Institute" title="Peabody Institute">Peabody Institute</a> is generally considered one of the most prestigious conservatories in the country, along with <a href="/wiki/Juilliard" title="Juilliard" class="mw-redirect">Juilliard</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Institute" title="Curtis Institute" class="mw-redirect">Curtis Institute</a>.</p> 
     <p>Johns Hopkins is ranked the #1 Social Media College by StudentAdvisor.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_100_Social_Media_Colleges_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_100_Social_Media_Colleges-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> Several university departments have been known to actively engage on various social media platforms such as Blogs, Facebook, Twitter, YouTube, and Flickr to reach prospective students, current students, and alumni.<sup id="cite_ref-Top_100_Social_Media_Colleges:_Johns_Hopkins_University_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Top_100_Social_Media_Colleges:_Johns_Hopkins_University-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The Johns Hopkins University Library system houses more than 3.6 million volumes.<sup id="cite_ref-American_Library_Association_Fact_Sheet_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-American_Library_Association_Fact_Sheet-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> It includes ten main divisions: the Sheridan Libraries at Homewood, the Welch Medical Library, the Medical Institution Libraries, the School of Nursing Library, Abraham M. Lilienfeld Library at the Bloomberg School, Friedheim Music Library at the Peabody Institute, the Carey Business School and School of Education libraries, the School of Advanced International Studies Libraries (Sydney R. and Elsa W. Mason Library and Bologna Center Library), the R.E. Gibson Library at the Applied Physics Laboratory Library and other minor satellite locations, as well as the archives.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg/220px-JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg/330px-JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg/440px-JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JHU_Eisenhower_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         <a href="/wiki/Milton_S._Eisenhower_Library" title="Milton S. Eisenhower Library" class="mw-redirect">Milton S. Eisenhower Library</a>
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Milton_S._Eisenhower_Library">Milton S. Eisenhower Library</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Milton S. Eisenhower Library">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Milton_S._Eisenhower_Library" title="Milton S. Eisenhower Library" class="mw-redirect">Milton S. Eisenhower Library</a>, located on the <a href="/wiki/Homewood_campus" title="Homewood campus" class="mw-redirect">Homewood campus</a>, is the main library. It was built in the 1960s. It houses over 2.6 million volumes and over 20,000 journal subscriptions. The Eisenhower Library is a member of the university's Sheridan Libraries encompassing collections at the Albert D. Hutzler Reading Room (called &quot;The Hut&quot; by students) in Gilman Hall, the John Work Garrett Library at Evergreen House, and the George Peabody Library at Mount Vernon Place. Together these collections provide the major research library resources for the university, serving Johns Hopkins academic programs worldwide. The library was named for <a href="/wiki/Milton_S._Eisenhower" title="Milton S. Eisenhower">Milton S. Eisenhower</a>, former president of the university and brother of former U.S. president <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a>. JHU's library was previously housed in Gilman Hall, and other smaller departmental libraries throughout the Homewood campus.<sup id="cite_ref-gil_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gil-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Only two of the Eisenhower library's six stories are above ground, though the architects designed the building so that every level has windows and natural light. The design accords with a bit of traditional campus lore that no structure can be taller than Gilman Hall, the oldest academic building ( although no written rule limits building height). In December 2008, an addition directly to the south of the library was announced. The six-and-a-half-story expansion will be named the Brody Learning Commons in honor of University President <a href="/wiki/William_R._Brody" title="William R. Brody">William R. Brody</a> and will function as a &quot;?collaborative learning space.&quot; It successfully opened on August 13, 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_Gazette_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_Gazette-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Home_Stretch_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Home_Stretch-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brody_Learning_Commons">Brody Learning Commons</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Brody Learning Commons">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
     <p>The Sheridan Libraries' Brody Learning Commons is the kind of 21st century library space that students need, where they can collaborate; research, read and study; tap into electronic resources; and learn to be scholars and critical thinkers. The building is named to honor former Johns Hopkins University president <a href="/wiki/William_R._Brody" title="William R. Brody">William R. Brody</a> and his wife, Wendy.<sup id="cite_ref-JHU_News_Releases_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JHU_News_Releases-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The four-story building, opened in August 2012, connects to the 1964 <a href="/wiki/Milton_S._Eisenhower_Library" title="Milton S. Eisenhower Library" class="mw-redirect">Milton S. Eisenhower Library</a> on all floors and includes high ceilings and light wells to provide natural light throughout the building. The facility features a robust technology infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-JHU_News_Releases_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JHU_News_Releases-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The technology-rich Learning Commons includes group study spaces, seminar rooms, and a state-of-the-art lab designed to integrate the role of scientists into the field of paper and manuscript conservation. The Rare Books and Manuscripts collection is on prominent physical display, supplemented by digital presentation of materials that allows users to compare and contrast different editions of rare documents in virtual and physical form. An atrium, which provides a transition between Brody and the Library, allows natural light to reach the lower levels of the Library while providing a civic space for the Learning Commons and the library community.<sup id="cite_ref-Shepley_Bulfinch_BLC_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shepley_Bulfinch_BLC-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Brody Learning Commons was designed by <a href="/wiki/Shepley_Bulfinch" title="Shepley Bulfinch">Shepley Bulfinch</a> and built by Lewis Contractors. It is an energy-efficient building, built according to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Green_Building_Council" title="United States Green Building Council" class="mw-redirect">United States Green Building Council</a> guidelines, and is the first new construction on the university's Homewood campus to achieve <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> Silver certification. The facility is open 24/7.<sup id="cite_ref-JHU_News_Releases_87-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JHU_News_Releases-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The opportunity to participate in important research is one of the distinguishing characteristics of Hopkins' undergraduate education. About 80 percent of undergraduates perform independent research, often alongside top researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-Carnegie_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carnegie-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_News_Release_.E2.80.93_JHU_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_News_Release_.E2.80.93_JHU-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> In FY 2009, Johns Hopkins received $1.856 billion in federal research grants?more than any other US university.<sup id="cite_ref-nsf09_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsf09-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Thirty-seven (37) <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners have been affiliated with the university as alumni or faculty members.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Johns_Hopkins_University:_Nobel_Prize_Winners_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Johns_Hopkins_University:_Nobel_Prize_Winners-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> JHU views its academic strengths as being in art history, biological, physical and other natural sciences, biomedical engineering, creative writing, English, history, economics, international studies, medicine, music, neuroscience, nursing, political theory, public health, public policy, and the <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Between 1999 and 2009, Johns Hopkins was among the most cited institutions in the world. It attracted nearly 1,222,166 citations and produced 54,022 papers under its name, ranking <sup>#</sup>3 globally (after <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">Max Planck Society</a>) in the number of <i>total</i> citations published in Thomson Reuters-indexed journals over 22 fields in America.<sup id="cite_ref-ScienceWatch.com_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ScienceWatch.com-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In FY 2000, Johns Hopkins received $95.4 million in research grants from the <a href="/wiki/National_Aeronautics_and_Space_Administration" title="National Aeronautics and Space Administration" class="mw-redirect">National Aeronautics and Space Administration</a> (NASA), making it the leading recipient of NASA <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> funding.<sup id="cite_ref-JHU_NASA_R.26D_2000_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JHU_NASA_R.26D_2000-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> In FY 2002, Hopkins became the first university to cross the $1 billion threshold on either list, recording $1.14 billion in total research and $1.023 billion in federally sponsored research. In FY 2008, Johns Hopkins University performed $1.68 billion in science, medical and engineering research, making it the leading U.S. academic institution in total R&amp;D spending for the 30th year in a row, according to a <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> (NSF) ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-ascribe_oct09_r.26d_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ascribe_oct09_r.26d-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> These totals include grants and expenditures of JHU's Applied Physics Laboratory in Laurel, Maryland. The Johns Hopkins University also offers the &quot;Center for Talented Youth&quot; program?a nonprofit organization dedicated to identifying and developing the talents of the most promising K-12 grade students worldwide. As part of the Johns Hopkins University, the &quot;Center for Talented Youth&quot; or CTY helps fulfill the university's mission of preparing students to make significant future contributions to the world.<sup id="cite_ref-nsf09_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nsf09-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_centers_and_institutes">Research centers and institutes</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Research centers and institutes">edit</a>]</span></h3>

           <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Divisional">Divisional</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Divisional">edit</a>]</span></h4> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a> (28)<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_Medicine:_Research_Centers_.26_CORE_Facilities_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_Medicine:_Research_Centers_.26_CORE_Facilities-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Bloomberg_School_of_Public_Health" title="Johns Hopkins Bloomberg School of Public Health">School of Public Health</a> (70)<sup id="cite_ref-Research_and_Centers_at_the_School_of_Public_Health_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Research_and_Centers_at_the_School_of_Public_Health-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Nursing" title="Johns Hopkins School of Nursing">School of Nursing</a> (2)<sup id="cite_ref-jhmi_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jhmi-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_School_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Johns Hopkins University School of Arts and Sciences">School of Arts and Sciences</a> (27)<sup id="cite_ref-Programs.2C_Centers_.26_Institutes_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Programs.2C_Centers_.26_Institutes-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Paul_H._Nitze_School_of_Advanced_International_Studies" title="Paul H. Nitze School of Advanced International Studies">School of Advanced International Studies</a> (17)<sup id="cite_ref-SAIS_Research_Centers_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAIS_Research_Centers-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Whiting_School_of_Engineering" title="Whiting School of Engineering">School of Engineering</a> (16)<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_University_Whiting_School_of_Engineering_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_University_Whiting_School_of_Engineering-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></li>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Johns_Hopkins_University_Press">Johns Hopkins University Press</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Johns Hopkins University Press">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_Press" title="Johns Hopkins University Press">Johns Hopkins University Press</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Johns Hopkins University Press is the publishing division of the Johns Hopkins University. It was founded in 1878 and holds the distinction of being the oldest continuously running <a href="/wiki/University_press" title="University press" class="mw-redirect">university press</a> in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-About_the_Press_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_the_Press-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> To date the Press has published more than 6,000 titles and currently publishes 65 scholarly periodicals and over 200 new books each year. Since 1993, the Johns Hopkins University Press has run <a href="/wiki/Project_MUSE" title="Project MUSE">Project MUSE</a>, an online collection of over 250 full?text, peer?reviewed journals in the humanities and social sciences. The Press also houses the Hopkins Fulfilment Services (HFS), which handles distribution for a number of university presses and publishers. Taken together, the three divisions of the Press?Books, Journals (including MUSE) and HFS?make it one of the largest of America's university presses.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JHUQuad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/JHUQuad.jpg/220px-JHUQuad.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/JHUQuad.jpg/330px-JHUQuad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/JHUQuad.jpg/440px-JHUQuad.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JHUQuad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         Students gather under the holidays lights at the yearly &quot;Lighting of the Quad&quot;, a Hopkins tradition
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Johns Hopkins Student Government Association represents undergraduates in campus issues and projects. It is elected annually.<sup id="cite_ref-About_Us_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-About_Us-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Blueprints for a new programming board called The Hopkins Organization for Programming (&quot;The HOP&quot;) were drawn up during the summer and fall of 2006.</p> 
     <p>In addition <a href="/wiki/Charles_Village,_Baltimore" title="Charles Village, Baltimore">Charles Village</a>, the region of North Baltimore surrounding the university, has undergone several restoration projects, and the university has gradually bought the property around the school for additional student housing and dormitories. <i>The Charles Village Project</i>, scheduled for completion in 2008, brought new commercial spaces to the neighborhood. The project included Charles Commons, a new, modern residence hall that includes popular retail franchises.<sup id="cite_ref-Charles_Commons_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Charles_Commons-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-einsteinbros_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-einsteinbros-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Hopkins invested in improving campus life with an arts complex in 2001, the Mattin Center, and a three?story sports facility, the O'Connor Recreation Center. The large on?campus dining facilities at Homewood were renovated in the summer of 2006.</p> 
     <p>Quality of life is enriched by the proximity of neighboring academic institutions, including <a href="/wiki/Loyola_College_in_Maryland" title="Loyola College in Maryland" class="mw-redirect">Loyola College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Institute_College_of_Art" title="Maryland Institute College of Art">Maryland Institute College of Art (MICA)</a>, <a href="/wiki/UMBC" title="UMBC" class="mw-redirect">UMBC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goucher_College" title="Goucher College">Goucher College</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Towson_University" title="Towson University">Towson University</a>, as well as nearby <a href="/wiki/Inner_Harbor" title="Inner Harbor">Inner Harbor</a>.</p> 
     <p>Annually, the Johns Hopkins Spring Fair is held on the Homewood campus over a three-day weekend in mid-to-late April. Food, arts and crafts, and non?profit vendors, along with a popular musical act and various other activities attract nearly 25,000 people from the greater Baltimore?Washington area. The Spring Fair is the largest entirely student?run fair in the country.</p> 
     <p>Since 1972, <a href="/wiki/The_Johns_Hopkins_Outdoors_Club" title="The Johns Hopkins Outdoors Club">the Johns Hopkins Outdoors Club</a>, or JHOC, has organized weekend trips for students looking to experience the outdoors. Along with Outdoor Pursuits, an arm of the University's Rec Center, JHOC offers students the opportunity to participate in activities such as canoeing, kayaking, caving, and mountain biking.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:AMRs_at_JHU.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/AMRs_at_JHU.JPG/170px-AMRs_at_JHU.JPG" width="170" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/AMRs_at_JHU.JPG/255px-AMRs_at_JHU.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/AMRs_at_JHU.JPG/340px-AMRs_at_JHU.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:AMRs_at_JHU.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <center>
         Freshman Residence Hall at JHU
        </center> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Living on campus is required for first- and second-year students, except for commuter students who live with a parent or legal guardian.<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_Freshman_Room_Selection_Brochure_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_Freshman_Room_Selection_Brochure-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> Housing is not guaranteed for juniors or seniors at Johns Hopkins.</p> 
     <p>Freshmen housing is centered around Freshman Quad, which consists of three major residence hall complexes: The Alumni Memorial Residences (AMR I and AMR II), Building A and Building B.<sup id="cite_ref-Freshman_Residence_Halls_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freshman_Residence_Halls-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> AMR I was built in 1923 and includes Royce, Sylvester, Vincent, Willard, Wilson and Wood houses; AMR II in 1954, holding Adams, Baker, Clark, Gildersleeve, Griffin, Hollander, Jennings, Lazear houses.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> While each house has its own outside entrance, there are no dividers indoors that distinguish them. In 1983, Buildings A and B were added to Freshmen Quad.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They have not yet been dedicated. Freshmen are also housed in Wolman Hall and the terrace floor of McCoy Hall, located on the other side of North Charles Street.<sup id="cite_ref-Freshman_Residence_Halls_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freshman_Residence_Halls-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Freshman enter a housing lottery in their spring semester to determine where they will live during their sophomore year. Juniors and seniors may choose between entering the campus housing lottery or moving into nearby apartments or row houses. They occupy one of four buildings.<sup id="cite_ref-Freshman_Room_Selection_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freshman_Room_Selection-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The first, McCoy Hall, is located next to Wolman Hall on North Charles Street. McCoy Hall is predominantly composed of sophomores and transfer students.<sup id="cite_ref-Oncampus:_Buildings_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oncampus:_Buildings-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Apartment-style housing is offered in the Bradford Apartments, one block east of campus on St. Paul Street, and in the Homewood Apartments, two blocks south on North Charles Street.<sup id="cite_ref-Freshman_Room_Selection_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freshman_Room_Selection-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The last is Charles Commons, the newest and largest university?owned dormitory, located at the corner of North Charles and East 33rd. It was completed in 2006 to house 618 students and represented a major step by the university towards offering on?campus housing to students.<sup id="cite_ref-Oncampus:_Buildings_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oncampus:_Buildings-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> Charles Commons consists of two 11?story towers connected by a bridge, residential suites and features a ballroom, fitness center and several conference rooms. Nolan's on 33rd, a dining hall specializing in dinner services, is also located in the building.<sup id="cite_ref-Oncampus:_Buildings_109-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oncampus:_Buildings-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>JHU rents several buildings on North Charles Street to house students when necessary. At full capacity, dormitory buildings can house approximately 60% of undergraduates.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Privately?owned apartment buildings around Homewood are usually filled with Hopkins upperclassmen, so despite the lack of university?owned dormitories, housing is available.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fraternities_and_sororities">Fraternities and sororities</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Fraternities and sororities">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University Office of Greek Life recognizes thirteen fraternities and eight sororities, which include approximately 25% of the student body. Greek life has been a part of the university culture since 1877, when <a href="/wiki/Beta_Theta_Pi" title="Beta Theta Pi">Beta Theta Pi</a> fraternity became the first to form a chapter on campus. Sororities arrived at Hopkins in 1982. As with all Hopkins programs, Greek discrimination on the basis of &quot;marital status, pregnancy, race, color, ethnicity, national origin, age, disability, religion, sexual orientation, veteran status&quot; is prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-Equity_Compliance_and_Education_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Equity_Compliance_and_Education-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> JHU also has an anti?hazing policy<sup id="cite_ref-Hazing_Information_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hazing_Information-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and prohibits alcohol at recruitment activities.<sup id="cite_ref-IFC_Recruitment_Rules_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IFC_Recruitment_Rules-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Hopkins does not permit &quot;city?wide&quot; chapters, and requires all members of a JHU recognized fraternity or sorority to be a JHU student.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Greek_Life_Policies_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Greek_Life_Policies-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of spring 2011, 1,208 students were members of one of Hopkins' fraternities or sororities. The All?Greek Average <a href="/wiki/GPA" title="GPA" class="mw-redirect">GPA</a> was 3.31, above the undergraduate average GPA.<sup id="cite_ref-Greek_Grade_Information.2C_Spring_2011_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Greek_Grade_Information.2C_Spring_2011-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In spring 2010 the university was considering construction of a &quot;fraternity row&quot; of houses to consolidate the groups on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-Hopkins_Greek_Life_considers_fraternity_row_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hopkins_Greek_Life_considers_fraternity_row-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>All Johns Hopkins fraternities and sororities belong to one of four Councils: the <b>Inter?Fraternity Council</b>, the <b><a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a></b>, the <b><a href="/wiki/National_Pan-Hellenic_Council" title="National Pan-Hellenic Council">National Pan-Hellenic Council</a></b> and the <b>Multicultural Council</b>.</p> 
     <p>The Inter?Fraternity Council includes eleven fraternities:<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_Inter.E2.80.93Fraternity_Council_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_Inter.E2.80.93Fraternity_Council-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a> fraternity, <i>chapter founded 1889.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a> fraternity, <i>Psi chapter founded 1936. Jewish interest.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Beta_Theta_Pi" title="Beta Theta Pi">Beta Theta Pi</a> fraternity, <i>Alpha Chi chapter founded 1877.</i><sup id="cite_ref-Beta_Theta_Pi_at_Hopkins_University_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beta_Theta_Pi_at_Hopkins_University-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Phi_Epsilon" title="Lambda Phi Epsilon">Lambda Phi Epsilon</a> fraternity, <i>Upsilon chapter founded 1994. Asian?American interest.</i><sup id="cite_ref-Lambda_Phi_Epsilon_Fraternity_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambda_Phi_Epsilon_Fraternity-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a> fraternity, <i>Maryland Delta chapter founded 2008.</i></li> 
      <li>FIJI ? <a href="/wiki/Phi_Gamma_Delta" title="Phi Gamma Delta">Phi Gamma Delta</a> fraternity, <i>Beta Mu chapter founded 1891.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Psi" title="Phi Kappa Psi">Phi Kappa Psi</a> fraternity, <i>Maryland Alpha chapter founded 1879.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Pi_Kappa_Alpha" title="Pi Kappa Alpha">Pi Kappa Alpha</a> fraternity, <i>Iota Tau chapter founded 1994.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha_Epsilon" title="Sigma Alpha Epsilon">Sigma Alpha Epsilon</a> fraternity, <i>Maryland Phi chapter founded 1994.</i></li> 
      <li>?? ? <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a> fraternity, <i>Kappa Upsilon chapter founded 2004.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Phi_Epsilon" title="Sigma Phi Epsilon">Sigma Phi Epsilon</a> fraternity, <i>Maryland Alpha chapter founded 1929.</i></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The National Panhellenic Conference includes four sororities:<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_National_Pan-Hellenic_Council_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_National_Pan-Hellenic_Council-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li>?? ? <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a> sorority, <i>Zeta Omicron chapter founded 1982.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a> sorority, <i>Eta Epsilon chapter founded 1999.</i></li> 
      <li>?M ? <a href="/wiki/Phi_Mu" title="Phi Mu">Phi Mu</a> sorority, <i>Gamma Tau chapter founded 1982.</i></li> 
      <li>?B? ? <a href="/wiki/Pi_Beta_Phi" title="Pi Beta Phi">Pi Beta Phi</a> sorority, <i>Maryland Gamma chartered November 20, 2010.</i></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>The National Pan?Hellenic Council includes two historically African?American groups:<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_National_Pan-Hellenic_Council5_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_National_Pan-Hellenic_Council5-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

     </ul> 
     <p>The <b>Multicultural Council</b> includes four groups:<sup id="cite_ref-Multicultural_Greeks_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Multicultural_Greeks-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JHU-Aerial.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JHU-Aerial.JPG/220px-JHU-Aerial.JPG" width="220" height="85" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JHU-Aerial.JPG/330px-JHU-Aerial.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/JHU-Aerial.JPG/440px-JHU-Aerial.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JHU-Aerial.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Johns Hopkins University Main Campus at Homewood
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li>???? ? <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Kappa Delta Phi">Alpha Kappa Delta Phi</a> sorority, <i>associate chapter founded 1997. Asian?American interest.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Delta_Xi_Phi" title="Delta Xi Phi">Delta Xi Phi</a> sorority, <i>Lambda chapter founded 2003. Multicultural interest.</i></li> 
      <li>IN? ? <a href="/wiki/Iota_Nu_Delta" title="Iota Nu Delta">Iota Nu Delta</a> fraternity, <i>chapter founded 2008. South Asian interest.</i></li> 
      <li>??? ? <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Omicron_Pi" title="Sigma Omicron Pi">Sigma Omicron Pi</a> sorority, <i>Lambda chapter founded 2002. Asian?American interest.</i></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Delta_Phi" title="Delta Phi">Delta Phi</a> Fraternity, also known as St. Elmo's, maintains a chapter exclusive to students at Johns Hopkins, though it is not recognized by the Office of Greek Life.</p> 
     <p>Unrecognized <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Alpha" title="Alpha Kappa Alpha">Alpha Kappa Alpha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Theta" title="Delta Sigma Theta">Delta Sigma Theta</a> African?American interest sororities often recruit Johns Hopkins undergraduates, in their city?wide chapters. <a href="/wiki/Delta_Sigma_Theta" title="Delta Sigma Theta">Delta Sigma Theta</a> was the first <b>National Pan?Hellenic Council</b> member to charter on the campus in 1976, as well as the first sorority of any kind on the JHU campus.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, a <a href="/wiki/National_Panhellenic_Conference" title="National Panhellenic Conference">National Panhellenic Conference</a> (NPC) sorority, was disbanded by its national headquarters on April 14, 2009 after twelve years on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-Theta_to_be_disbanded_indefinitely_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theta_to_be_disbanded_indefinitely-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> The removal was due to repeated risk management violations.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>In March 2010, Johns Hopkins University officially opened for NPC extension.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In May 2010, the University Panhellenic Council selected <a href="/wiki/Pi_Beta_Phi" title="Pi Beta Phi">Pi Beta Phi</a>, which opened in the fall of 2010.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-New_sorority_to_begin_recruitment_this_fall_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_sorority_to_begin_recruitment_this_fall-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Recruitment for Inter?Fraternity Council and Panhellenic Conference fraternities and sororities takes place during the spring semester for freshmen, though some groups recruit upperclassmen during the fall semester.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> All participants must have completed one semester and must be in good academic standing.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <p>Many of the fraternities maintain houses off campus, but no sororities do.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Baltimore City allows housing to be zoned specifically for use as a fraternity or sorority house, but in practice this zoning code has not been awarded for at least 50 years.<sup class="Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Only Sigma Phi Epsilon's building has this zoning code due to its consistent ownership since the 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-Baltimore_Zoning_Laws_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baltimore_Zoning_Laws-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_publications">Student publications</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Student publications">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:GilmanHall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/GilmanHall.JPG/170px-GilmanHall.JPG" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/GilmanHall.JPG/255px-GilmanHall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/GilmanHall.JPG/340px-GilmanHall.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:GilmanHall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Gilman Hall, Center for the Humanities
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Hopkins has many student publications.</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Johns_Hopkins_News-Letter" title="The Johns Hopkins News-Letter">The Johns Hopkins News-Letter</a></i>, founded in 1896, is one of the oldest continuously published weekly college newspapers in the nation with a press run of 5,200.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Johns_Hopkins_News.E2.80.93Letter_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Johns_Hopkins_News.E2.80.93Letter-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> The News-Letter won an Associated Collegiate Press Newspaper Pacemaker award for four?year, non?daily college newspapers in 2007.</li> 
      <li><i><a href="/wiki/JHU_Politik" title="JHU Politik">JHU Politik</a></i>, founded in 2008 as the University's only bi-partisan political publication, produces a weekly magazine, The Politik Press. The Politik Press contains student written op-eds and interviews with professors, professionals and experts in various political fields. Every semester JHU Politik publishes a special issue to highlight diverse perspectives on singular topics. JHU Politik is also responsible for numerous speakers events on campus as well as more informal discussions and conversations that take place throughout the academic year.</li> 
      <li><i>Epidemic Proportions</i> is the university's public health research journal, designed to highlight JHU research and field work in public health. Combining research and scholarship, the journal seeks to capture the breadth and depth of the JHU undergraduate public health experience.<sup id="cite_ref-Epidemic_Proportions_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Epidemic_Proportions-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>Thoroughfare,</i> <i>Zeniada</i> and <i>j.mag</i> are literary magazines. <i>Prometheus</i> is the undergraduate philosophy journal.<sup id="cite_ref-Prometheus_.E2.80.93_Johns_Hopkins_Undergraduate_Journal_of_Philosophy_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prometheus_.E2.80.93_Johns_Hopkins_Undergraduate_Journal_of_Philosophy-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>Frame of Reference</i> is an annual magazine that focuses on film and film culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Johns_Hopkins_Film_Festival_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Johns_Hopkins_Film_Festival-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>The New Diplomat</i> is the multi?disciplinary international relations journal. <i>Foundations</i> is the undergraduate history journal.<sup id="cite_ref-Foundations_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Foundations-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>Am&eacute;ricas</i> is the Latin American Studies journal.<sup id="cite_ref-Am.C3.A9ricas_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Am.C3.A9ricas-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>Argot</i> is the undergraduate anthropology journal.<sup id="cite_ref-Argot_Research_Journal_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Argot_Research_Journal-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>The Triple Helix</i> is the university's journal to address issues concerning science, law and society.</li> 
      <li><i>Perspectives</i> is the official newsletter of the <i>Black Student Union</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Black_Student_Union_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Black_Student_Union-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>The Black &amp; Blue Jay</i> is among the nation's oldest campus humor magazines. It was founded in 1920.<sup id="cite_ref-jhu6_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jhu6-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i>The Johns Hopkins News?Letter</i>, the magazine's name led the News?Letter to first use the moniker Blue Jays to refer to a Hopkins athletic team in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-Where_did_they_get_that_darn_Blue_Jay.3F_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Where_did_they_get_that_darn_Blue_Jay.3F-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> While the magazine enjoyed popularity among students, it received repeated opposition from the university administration, reportedly for its vulgar humor. In October 1934, Dean Edward R. Berry removed financial support for the magazine; without funding, the magazine continued under the name <i>The Blue Jay</i> until Berry threatened to expel the editors in 1939. The magazine had a revival in 1984, and has appeared intermittently since then.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Black_and_Blue_Jay_returns_to_campus_with_a_vengeance_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Black_and_Blue_Jay_returns_to_campus_with_a_vengeance-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li><i>The Hopkins Donkey</i> was a political newspaper with a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> perspective on international, national and state?wide political topics. It is now defunct.</li> 
      <li><i>The Carrollton Record</i> was a political newspaper with an <a href="/wiki/American_conservatism" title="American conservatism" class="mw-redirect">American conservative</a> perspective on campus and city?wide politics.<sup id="cite_ref-tcrecord.com_homepage_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcrecord.com_homepage-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> Like the Hopkins Donkey, it is now defunct.</li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student.E2.80.93Run_businesses">Student?Run businesses</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Student?Run businesses">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Hopkins Student Enterprises (HSE)<sup id="cite_ref-johnshopkins_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnshopkins-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> is a venture capital fund and umbrella organization with the goal of fostering innovation and facilitating resources and mentorship to student entrepreneurs. Currently, five businesses are in operation:<sup id="cite_ref-Young_Money_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Young_Money-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Hopkins_Consulting_Agency" title="Hopkins Consulting Agency">Hopkins Consulting Agency</a> (HCA)?Business and technology consulting company that prepares technology commercialization reports and business plans.</li> 
      <li>Hopkins Student Movers (HSM)?Moving and storage company that serves JHU faculty, staff, and students and the broader Baltimore community.<sup id="cite_ref-johnshopkins7_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johnshopkins7-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>Hopkins Creative Design (HCD)?Full service graphic design company.<sup id="cite_ref-Hopkins_Creative_Services_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hopkins_Creative_Services-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Blue Jay Cleaners - Student janitorial service for all on-campus and select off campus residence halls.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
      <li>Blue Jay Boxes - Care package and cake delivery business for Charles Village and the surrounding neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Jay_Head.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Blue_Jay_Head.svg/220px-Blue_Jay_Head.svg.png" width="220" height="257" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Blue_Jay_Head.svg/330px-Blue_Jay_Head.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Blue_Jay_Head.svg/440px-Blue_Jay_Head.svg.png 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Jay_Head.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Athletics logo
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays">Johns Hopkins Blue Jays</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Athletic teams are called Blue Jays. Even though <a href="/wiki/Sable_(heraldry)" title="Sable (heraldry)">sable</a> and <a href="/wiki/Or_(heraldry)" title="Or (heraldry)">gold</a> are used for <a href="/wiki/Academic_dress" title="Academic dress">academic robes</a>, the university's athletic colors are <a href="/wiki/Columbia_blue" title="Columbia blue">Columbia blue</a> (PMS 284) and <a href="/wiki/Black" title="Black">black</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Official_Athletic_Site_of_Johns_Hopkins_University_.E2.80.93_Athletic_Quick_Facts_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Official_Athletic_Site_of_Johns_Hopkins_University_.E2.80.93_Athletic_Quick_Facts-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> Hopkins celebrates <a href="/wiki/Homecoming" title="Homecoming">Homecoming</a> in the spring to coincide with the height of the <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a> season. The Men's and Women's lacrosse teams are in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> (NCAA) <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a>. Other teams are in <a href="/wiki/Division_III_(NCAA)" title="Division III (NCAA)">Division III</a> and participate in the <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Conference" title="Centennial Conference">Centennial Conference</a>. JHU is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse_Museum_and_National_Hall_of_Fame" title="Lacrosse Museum and National Hall of Fame">Lacrosse Museum and National Hall of Fame</a>, maintained by <a href="/wiki/US_Lacrosse" title="US Lacrosse">US Lacrosse</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_lacrosse">Men's lacrosse</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Men's lacrosse">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays men's lacrosse">Johns Hopkins Blue Jays men's lacrosse</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:JHU_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/JHU_001.jpg/220px-JHU_001.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/JHU_001.jpg/330px-JHU_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d8/JHU_001.jpg/440px-JHU_001.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:JHU_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Johns Hopkins Men's Lacrosse at 
        <a href="/wiki/Homewood_Field" title="Homewood Field">Homewood Field</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The school's most prominent team is its men's <a href="/wiki/Lacrosse" title="Lacrosse">lacrosse</a> team. The team does not belong to a conference. The team has won 44 national titles ? nine Division I (2007, 2005, 1987, 1985, 1984, 1980, 1979, 1978, 1974), 29 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Intercollegiate_Lacrosse_Association" title="United States Intercollegiate Lacrosse Association">United States Intercollegiate Lacrosse Association</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_States_Intercollegiate_Lacrosse_Association" title="United States Intercollegiate Lacrosse Association">USILA</a>), and six Intercollegiate Lacrosse Association (ILA) titles. Hopkins' primary national rivals are <a href="/wiki/Princeton_Tigers_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Princeton Tigers men's lacrosse">Princeton University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syracuse_Orange_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Syracuse Orange men's lacrosse">Syracuse University</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Cavaliers_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Virginia Cavaliers men's lacrosse">University of Virginia</a>; its primary intrastate rivals are <a href="/wiki/Loyola_Greyhounds_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Loyola Greyhounds men's lacrosse">Loyola University Maryland</a> (competing in what is called the &quot;<a href="/wiki/Charles_Street_Massacre" title="Charles Street Massacre" class="mw-redirect">Charles Street Massacre</a>&quot;), <a href="/wiki/Towson_Tigers_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Towson Tigers men's lacrosse">Towson University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Navy_Midshipmen_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Navy Midshipmen men's lacrosse">United States Naval Academy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Maryland_Terrapins_men%27s_lacrosse" title="Maryland Terrapins men's lacrosse">University of Maryland</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins%E2%80%94Maryland_rivalry" title="Johns Hopkins?Maryland rivalry" class="mw-redirect">rivalry with Maryland</a> is the oldest. The schools have met 103 times since 1899, twice in playoff matches.</p> 
     <p>On June 3, 2013, it was announced that the Blue Jays would join the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a> for lacrosse when that league begins sponsoring the sport in the 2015 season (2014?15 school year).</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_lacrosse">Women's lacrosse</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Women's lacrosse">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Blue_Jays_women%27s_lacrosse" title="Johns Hopkins Blue Jays women's lacrosse">Johns Hopkins Blue Jays women's lacrosse</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The women's team is a member of the <a href="/wiki/American_Lacrosse_Conference" title="American Lacrosse Conference">American Lacrosse Conference</a> (ALC). The team is developing into a top twenty team. The Lady Blue Jays were ranked number 19 in the 2008 Inside Lacrosse Women's DI Media Poll (ILWDIMP). They ranked number 8 in both the 2007 Intercollegiate Women's Lacrosse Coaches Association (IWLCA) Poll for Division I and the ILWDIMP. In 2006, they were ranked 14th in the ILWDIMP, in 2005, they were 11th, and, in 2004, they were 9th. However, recently the team has struggled and finished with a record of 5 wins and 12 losses in the 2009 season.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_teams">Other teams</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Other teams">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Hopkins has notable Division III Athletic teams. JHU Men's <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">Swimming</a> won three consecutive <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Championships" title="NCAA Championships" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Championships</a> in 1977, 1978, and 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-ncaa_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ncaa-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009?2010, Hopkins won 8 Centennial Conference titles in Women's Cross Country, Women's Track &amp; Field, Baseball, Men's and Women's Soccer, Football, and Men's and Women's Tennis. The Women's Cross Country team became the first women's team at Hopkins to achieve a #1 National ranking. In 2006?2007 teams won Centennial Conference titles in Baseball, Men's and Women's Soccer, Men's and Women's Tennis and Men's Basketball. Women's soccer won their Centennial Conference title for 7 consecutive years from 2005-2011.</p> 
     <p>Hopkins has an acclaimed <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">fencing</a> team, which ranked in the top three Division III teams in the past few years and in both 2008 and 2007 defeated the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">University of North Carolina</a>, a Division I team. In 2008, they defeated UNC and won the MACFA championship.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">Swimming</a> team ranked highly in NCAA Division III for the last 10 years, most recently placing second at DIII Nationals in 2008. The Water Polo team was number one in Division III for several of the past years, playing a full schedule against Division I opponents. Hopkins also has a century-old rivalry with <a href="/wiki/McDaniel_College" title="McDaniel College">McDaniel College</a> (formerly Western Maryland College), playing the Green Terrors 83 times in football since the first game in 1894. In 2009 the football team reached the quarterfinals of the NCAA Division III tournament, with three tournament appearances since 2005. In 2008, the baseball team ranked second, losing in the final game of the DIII <a href="/wiki/College_World_Series" title="College World Series">College World Series</a> to <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Hartford" title="Trinity College, Hartford" class="mw-redirect">Trinity College</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2008_NCAA_Division_III_Baseball_Championship.2C_University_of_Wisconsin.E2.80.93Oshkosh_Titans_website_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2008_NCAA_Division_III_Baseball_Championship.2C_University_of_Wisconsin.E2.80.93Oshkosh_Titans_website-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Johns Hopkins squash team plays in the College Squash Association as a club team along with Division I and III varsity programs. In 2011-12m the squash team finished 30th in the ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni.2C_faculty_and_staff">Notable alumni, faculty and staff</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Notable alumni, faculty and staff">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Johns_Hopkins_University_people" title="List of Johns Hopkins University people">List of Johns Hopkins University people</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Leslie_Delatour" title="Leslie Delatour">Leslie Delatour</a> Former Governor of Haiti's central bank</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_laureates">Nobel laureates</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Nobel laureates">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_affiliated_with_Johns_Hopkins_University" title="List of Nobel laureates affiliated with Johns Hopkins University">List of Nobel laureates affiliated with Johns Hopkins University</a>
     </div> 
     <p>As of 2011, there have been 37 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel</a> Laureates who either attended the university as undergraduate or graduate students, or were faculty members.<sup id="cite_ref-WinnersList_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WinnersList-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>, who received his PhD from Johns Hopkins in 1886, was Hopkins' first affiliated laureate, winning the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-WinnersList_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WinnersList-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Peace1919_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Peace1919-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> Twenty-three laureates were faculty members, five earned PhDs, eight earned <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">M.D.s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Francis_Peyton_Rous" title="Francis Peyton Rous">Francis Peyton Rous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Rodbell" title="Martin Rodbell">Martin Rodbell</a> earned <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_degrees" title="Undergraduate degrees" class="mw-redirect">undergraduate degrees</a>.</p> 
     <p>Eighteen Johns Hopkins laureates have won the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-WinnersList_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WinnersList-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Four Nobel Prizes were shared by Johns Hopkins laureates: <a href="/wiki/George_Minot" title="George Minot">George Minot</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Whipple" title="George Whipple">George Whipple</a> won the 1934 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-Medicine1934_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medicine1934-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Erlanger" title="Joseph Erlanger">Joseph Erlanger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Spencer_Gasser" title="Herbert Spencer Gasser">Herbert Spencer Gasser</a> won the 1944 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-Medicine1944_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medicine1944-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Nathans" title="Daniel Nathans">Daniel Nathans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_O._Smith" title="Hamilton O. Smith">Hamilton O. Smith</a> won the 1978 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine,<sup id="cite_ref-Medicine1978_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medicine1978-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/David_H._Hubel" title="David H. Hubel">David H. Hubel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torsten_N._Wiesel" title="Torsten N. Wiesel" class="mw-redirect">Torsten N. Wiesel</a> won the 1981 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-Medicine1981_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medicine1981-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Two Johns Hopkins laureates won Nobel Prizes in Physics, <a href="/wiki/Riccardo_Giacconi" title="Riccardo Giacconi">Riccardo Giacconi</a> in 2002 <sup id="cite_ref-Physics_2002_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Physics_2002-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Riess" title="Adam Riess">Adam Riess</a> in 2011. <sup id="cite_ref-Physics_2011_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Physics_2011-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=Johns_Hopkins_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="noprint tright portal" style="border:solid #aaa 1px;margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;">
